[1:0:344,377] The Transportation Agency develops and  

[1:1:344,387] coordinates transportation policies and programs  

[1:2:344,397] to achieve the state's mobility, safety, and  

[1:3:344,407] environmental sustainability objectives. The  

[1:4:344,417] Agency oversees and coordinates the activities of  

[1:5:344,427] the following state entities: Department of  

[1:6:344,437] Transportation, California Transportation  

[1:7:344,447] Commission, High-Speed Rail Authority,  

[1:8:344,457] Department of Motor Vehicles, California Highway  

[1:9:344,466] Patrol, and the Board of Pilot Commissioners.

[1:0:178,39] 2600   California Transportation Commission  

[2:0:66,61] The California Transportation Commission is responsible for programming and allocating funds for the construction and  

[2:1:66,71] improvement of highways, passenger rail systems, and transit systems throughout California. The Commission advises and  

[2:2:66,81] assists the Transportation Agency and the Legislature in formulating and evaluating state policies and plans for California's  

[2:3:66,91] transportation programs. The Commission also initiates and develops state and federal transportation policies that seek to  

[2:4:66,101] secure financial stability for the state.

[5:0:66,192] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,212] 1800 - ADMINISTRATION OF THE CALIFORNIA TRANSPORTATION COMMISSION  

[7:0:66,232] This program reviews and adopts the State Transportation Improvement Program, the State Highway Operation and Protection  

[7:1:66,242] Program, the Active Transportation Program, the Local Partnership program, the Solutions for Congested Corridors Program,  

[7:2:66,253] the Trade Corridor Enhancement Program, and adopts the State Transportation Improvement Program Fund Estimate. The  

[7:3:66,263] program also approves city and county eligibility for a portion of the funding in the Local Streets and Roads Program.  

[7:4:66,273] Additionally, the program allocates transportation revenues and bond funds for highways, passenger rail systems, active  

[7:5:66,283] transportation, and transit system improvements in California. The program also collaborates with and provides guidance to  

[7:6:66,293] other state and local transportation agencies on a variety of transportation issues including planning, asset management, and  

[7:7:66,304] system improvements.  

[8:0:66,321] 1805 - CLEAN AIR AND TRANSPORTATION IMPROVEMENT  

[9:0:66,342] This program allocates Proposition 116 bond funds to the Department of Transportation, the Department of Parks and  

[9:1:66,352] Recreation, and local agencies that are used for the preservation, acquisition, construction, and improvement of rail  

[9:2:66,362] infrastructure, paratransit vehicles, bicycle facilities, water-borne ferry vessels and facilities, public transit, and the California  

[9:3:66,372] State Museum of Railroad Technology.

[7:0:66,249] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[8:0:65,268] • Transportation Infrastructure Package - The budget includes $1.3 billion in additional state and federal funds for priority  

[8:1:76,278] repairs on the state highway system, interregional transportation projects, and local road and bridge investments. 

[8:2:76,288] Additionally, the budget provides $500 million for additional Active Transportation Program projects and $300 million for state  

[8:3:76,298] and local climate adaptation projects.  

[8:4:65,315] • Clean California Initiative – The budget provides $475 million for the first year of a three-year effort to clean up garbage  

[8:5:76,325] statewide, beautify the state’s transportation network, educate the public about the harms of litter, and create long-lasting  

[8:6:76,335] litter deterrents.  

[9:0:65,351] • Capital Outlay Support – The budget provides an additional $107 million federal and 467 new positions to provide project  

[9:1:76,361] engineering and design support necessary to deliver transportation infrastructure projects, including environmental review  

[9:2:76,372] and mitigation, right-of-way acquisition, construction management, and oversight of external consultant services.

[5:0:66,366] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,386] 1830019 - AERONAUTICS  

[6:0:66,406] The Aeronautics Program supports California's aviation activities by promoting the safe and effective use of airports and  

[6:1:66,416] heliports. This program oversees safety compliance and provides engineering and financial assistance for safety and  

[6:2:66,427] infrastructure improvements. The division maintains the California Aviation System Plan, provides guidance for land use  

[6:3:66,437] compatibility in areas around airports, administers airport noise standards and regulations, and enhances goods movement to  

[6:4:66,447] and from airports through improved ground access.  

[6:5:66,465] 1835010 - CAPITAL OUTLAY SUPPORT  

[7:0:66,482] The Capital Outlay Support Program is responsible for developing capital projects on the state highway system and preparing  

[7:1:66,493] these for the construction phase. Functions of this program include the activities necessary to deliver construction projects,  

[7:2:66,503] such as engineering and design work, environmental studies, right-of-way acquisition, and construction inspection activities.  

[7:3:66,513] The program also oversees private contractors that undertake the direct construction work for projects.  

[7:4:66,531] 1835019 - CAPITAL OUTLAY PROJECTS  

[8:0:66,548] The Capital Outlay Projects Program funds capacity projects in the State Transportation Improvement Program and repair  

[8:1:66,559] projects in the State Highway Operations and Protection Program. Projects are programmed by Caltrans and funding is  

[8:2:66,569] allocated by the California Transportation Commission. Project funding is used for acquisition of right-of-way and for  

[8:3:66,579] construction.  

[8:4:66,597] 1835020 - LOCAL ASSISTANCE  

[9:0:66,614] The Local Assistance Program provides state and federal funds to over 600 cities, counties and regional agencies to improve  

[9:1:66,625] their transportation infrastructure or provide transportation services. The program also provides guidance, expertise, and  

[9:2:66,635] oversight of transportation projects to monitor compliance with state and federal requirements to ensure successful project  

[9:3:66,645] completion.  

[9:4:66,663] 1835029 - PROGRAM DEVELOPMENT  

[10:0:66,680] The Program Development Program assists the department in fully utilizing available state and federal transportation funds for  

[10:1:66,691] both the state highway and intercity rail systems. The Division of Research, Innovation and System Information provides  

[10:2:66,701] research and data solutions needed to make informed decisions that improve California's transportation system. The Division  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — TRN   10 

[1:0:471,13] TRANSPORTATION 

[2:0:168,32] 2660   Department of Transportation - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] of Transportation Programming produces the State Transportation Improvement Program, State Highway Operations and  

[3:1:66,79] Protection Program, and the Federal Statewide Transportation Improvement Program documents.  

[4:0:66,97] 1835038 - LEGAL  

[5:0:66,114] The Legal Program advises the department on federal and state statutes, regulations, and case law, and how those laws  

[5:1:66,124] impact Caltrans' policy makers, operational needs, and associated risks. Through the Legal program, Caltrans handles all of its  

[5:2:66,135] own legal affairs, including: real property acquisition and management, construction, environmental, personnel, tort litigation,  

[5:3:66,145] and other matters. The program handles over 1,400 active legal matters, issues, and litigation cases annually. The program  

[5:4:66,155] also provides the High Speed Rail Authority fully reimbursed eminent domain legal services.  

[6:0:66,173] 1835047 - OPERATIONS  

[7:0:66,190] The Operations Program establishes statewide policies and procedures related to traffic management, identifies and prioritizes  

[7:1:66,201] the programming of highway safety and operational improvement projects, and manages the Statewide Transportation and  

[7:2:66,211] Encroachment Permits programs. The program also supports efficient system operation by administering incident management  

[7:3:66,221] and traveler information programs, providing technical support to local agencies, responding to incidents on state highways,  

[7:4:66,231] and providing traffic design support for design engineers.  

[8:0:66,249] 1835056 - MAINTENANCE  

[9:0:66,267] The Maintenance Program preserves California's highways by maintaining and repairing the state highway system. The  

[9:1:66,277] program achieves its objectives through a fix-it first approach, including: (1) preventive and corrective pavement maintenance;  

[9:2:66,287] (2) bridge inspection, load rating, and maintenance; (3) culvert inspection and maintenance; and (4) maintenance and repair of  

[9:3:66,297] traffic management system field elements. In addition, the program strives to improve highway travel, safety, and the  

[9:4:66,307] environment through testing, research, and technology development.  

[10:0:66,325] 1840019 - STATE AND FEDERAL MASS TRANSIT  

[11:0:66,343] The State and Federal Mass Transit Program administers state and federal grants that provide funding for operating  

[11:1:66,353] assistance, capital improvements, and equipment to public transportation agencies. The program assists agencies with  

[11:2:66,363] purchasing buses, rolling stock, and ferries; supports commuter and urban rail services and waterborne ferry operations; and  

[11:3:66,373] assists in providing services accessible to the elderly and disabled. The program achieves its objectives through: (1)  

[11:4:66,384] management of state and federal capital and operations grant programs; (2) planning, support, and coordination of mass  

[11:5:66,394] transportation services; and (3) administering state bond programs and state funding that directly support public transportation  

[11:6:66,404] efforts.  

[12:0:66,422] 1840028 - INTERCITY RAIL PASSENGER PROGRAM  

[13:0:66,439] The Intercity Rail Passenger Program helps to reduce highway congestion and automobile fuel consumption while improving  

[13:1:66,450] air quality and environmental protection by providing leadership in the planning and implementation of a passenger rail  

[13:2:66,460] transportation system. The program achieves its objectives through the: (1) support and funding of the intercity rail lines  

[13:3:66,470] administered by the Joint Powers Authorities; (2) management of state and federal rail capital improvement programs; (3)  

[13:4:66,480] ownership of state passenger rail equipment; and (4) development of the California State Rail Plan.  

[14:0:66,498] 1845013 - STATEWIDE PLANNING  

[15:0:66,516] The Statewide Planning Program implements statewide transportation policy through coordinated planning at the federal, state,  

[15:1:66,526] regional, and local levels. The program prepares the long-range state transportation plan, provides long-range interregional  

[15:2:66,536] transportation system planning and transportation planning studies to inform the State Transportation Improvement Program,  

[15:3:66,546] and supports departmental policies and programs such as goods movement and climate action. The program also prepares the  

[15:4:66,556] Interregional Transportation Strategic Plan, which guides investment of the Interregional Improvement Program funds in the  

[15:5:66,567] State Transportation Improvement Program.  

[16:0:66,584] 1845022 - REGIONAL PLANNING  

[17:0:66,602] The Regional Planning Program implements statewide transportation policy through coordination at the regional level and  

[17:1:66,612] develops transportation plans and projects. The program develops long-range regional transportation plans and provides long-

[17:2:66,622] range transportation system analysis and transportation planning studies as input to regional transportation plans. The program  

[17:3:66,633] also prepares transportation planning studies to support Caltrans policies and programs such as air quality and smart mobility.  

[18:0:66,650] 1850010 - EQUIPMENT SERVICE PROGRAM  

[19:0:66,668] The Equipment Service Program provides mobile fleet equipment and services to other departmental programs through: (1)  

[19:1:66,678] purchasing fleet equipment and related components, (2) receiving, servicing, and equipping new units, (3) managing the fleet,  

[19:2:66,688] (4) repairing and maintaining the fleet, including payments for fuel and insurance, and (5) disposing of end-of-life fleet assets.  

[20:0:66,706] 1870 - OFFICE OF INSPECTOR GENERAL

[3:0:66,69] The Office of Inspector General Program delivers professional audits and investigative services that assist management in  

[3:1:66,79] accomplishing departmental goals and objectives, setting priorities and making efficient, effective, and financially responsible  

[3:2:66,89] transportation decisions, Additionally, the office informs the Director, the Secretary of Transportation, the Legislature, and the  

[3:3:66,99] California Transportation Commission on issues concerning fraud, improper activities or other serious abuses or deficiencies  

[3:4:66,109] relating to the expenditure of transportation funds or administration of Department programs and operations. Major activities  

[3:5:66,120] include audits of external entities, internal performance audits and investigations.  

[3:6:66,137] 9900100 - ADMINISTRATION

[4:1:66,165] facility operations and management, information technology, human resources, procurement and contracting, training,  

[4:2:66,175] workforce planning, and labor relations.

[0:0:66,13] TRANSPORTATION 

[1:0:412,13] 2021-22 STATE BUDGET — TRN   53 

[2:0:68,32] 2670   Board of Pilot Commissioners for the Bays of San Francisco, San Pablo, and 

[2:1:251,47] Suisun - Continued 

[3:0:66,79] The Board's responsibilities include training and licensing maritime pilots, establishing standards for pilot fitness, incident  

[3:1:66,89] investigation, approval of pilot boat acquisitions and improvements, oversight of the San Francisco Bar Pilot Pension Plan, and  

[3:2:66,99] providing pilotage fee rate recommendations to the Legislature. The seven members of the Board are appointed by the  

[3:3:66,109] Governor with the consent of the Senate, and the Secretary of the Transportation Agency is an ex-officio member. The Board  

[3:4:66,120] was established in California's first Legislative Session, and has been in continuous existence since 1850.  

[4:0:66,140] All of the operational and program expenses of the Board are funded by various surcharges set by the Board, and are paid by  

[4:1:66,150] the shipping companies that utilize services of Board-licensed maritime pilots. The Board Operations Surcharge funds the cost  

[4:2:66,160] of Board operations, and is set as a percentage of pilotage fees. Three separate surcharges are based upon ship movements  

[4:3:66,171] and fund a continuing education program for pilots, a pilot trainee training program, and the acquisition of navigation technology  

[4:4:66,181] for use by pilots. Two separate surcharges are based on the tonnage of the vessel that arrives or leaves the San Francisco Bay  

[4:5:66,191] and fund pilot boat acquisitions and improvements, and the San Francisco Bar Pilot Pension Plan.

[4:0:66,422] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:1:66,441] 2050 - TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT  

[5:0:66,462] The objectives of this program are to minimize deaths, injuries, and property losses due to traffic accidents; to reduce traffic  

[5:1:66,472] delays to the motoring public; to provide protection and assistance to the motoring public, state employees and property,  

[5:2:66,482] including protection of the State Capitol and the surrounding grounds, state constitutional officers, and visiting dignitaries; and  

[5:3:66,492] to curtail the potential for terrorist threats as part of broader state and federal homeland security efforts. These objectives are  

[5:4:66,502] achieved through both ground and flight operations.  

[5:5:66,520] 2055 - REGULATION AND INSPECTION  

[6:0:66,538] The CHP operates 55 commercial vehicle enforcement facilities statewide with the objectives of:  

[6:1:65,555] • Reducing the incidence of truck and bus accidents attributable to defective vehicle equipment, improper maintenance,  

[6:2:76,566] loading or securing of cargo, or disqualified drivers.  

[7:0:65,582] • Protecting the public from spills of hazardous materials or specially regulated loads, and from the improper operation of  

[7:1:76,592] specified vehicles such as ambulances and armored cars.  

[8:0:65,608] • Protecting farm workers transported in farm labor vehicles and children transported in school buses.  

[8:1:65,624] • Ensuring that proper registration fees are paid, and protecting highways from excessive vehicle weights.  

[8:2:66,642] 2060 - VEHICLE OWNERSHIP SECURITY  

[8:3:66,660] This program protects the public from vehicle theft through:  

[8:4:65,678] • Investigation and prosecution of the professional vehicle thief.  

[8:5:65,694] • Assistance and training of CHP and allied agency personnel.  

[9:0:65,710] • Prevention of vehicle theft through public awareness and coordination with the insurance, trucking, construction, auto

[8:0:66,354] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[9:0:66,373] The California Highway Patrol operates   nearly   500 facilities of varying types statewide, which include 8 field division offices,  

[9:1:66,383] 103 Area commands, 24 dispatch/communications centers, 39 commercial vehicle inspection facilities and platform scales, 8  

[9:2:66,393] air operations facilities, 33 resident posts, 267 remote telecommunication sites, a training academy, and various administrative  

[9:3:66,403] facilities.   These facilities, consisting of approximately 1.6 million gross square feet of state-owned properties and 742,000  

[9:4:66,414] gross square feet of leased properties, support the CHP's mission to provide the highest level of safety, service, and security to  

[9:5:66,424] the people of California.  

[10:0:66,461] MAJOR PROJECT CHANGES  

[11:0:66,480] The Budget Act includes $154.8 million General for the design-build phase of office replacement projects in Quincy, Baldwin  

[11:1:66,490] Park, and Santa Fe Springs, and for the initial phases of office replacement projects at Humboldt and Gold Run. The latter  

[11:2:66,501] projects will require $83.6 million in future years to complete.

[3:0:66,69] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,88] 2130 - VEHICLE/VESSEL IDENTIFICATION AND COMPLIANCE  

[4:0:66,109] This program establishes identification and ownership of vehicles and vessels of California residents, supports compliance with  

[4:1:66,119] various related laws, collects revenue for various state and local government programs, and provides information from vehicle  

[4:2:66,129] and vessel records to state and local agencies.  

[4:3:66,147] 2135 - DRIVER LICENSING AND PERSONAL IDENTIFICATION  

[5:0:66,167] This program evaluates the eligibility and ability of applicants for original and renewal driver licenses, issues driver licenses  

[5:1:66,177] and/or identification cards to those who meet specific criteria, provides information from driver license and identification card  

[5:2:66,187] records to state and local law enforcement agencies, and collects voter registration information.  

[5:3:66,205] 2140 - DRIVER SAFETY  

[6:0:66,226] This program promotes driver safety by monitoring, suspending, and revoking the driving privilege of unsafe licensed drivers  

[6:1:66,236] operating on public roadways.  

[6:2:66,253] 2145 - OCCUPATIONAL LICENSING AND INVESTIGATIVE SERVICES  

[7:0:66,271] This program enhances consumer protection by licensing and regulating motor vehicle-related businesses that provide services  

[7:1:66,281] connected to the sale and use of vehicles in California and enforces laws within the Department's jurisdiction by means of  

[7:2:66,292] criminal and administrative investigations.  

[7:3:66,309] 2150 - NEW MOTOR VEHICLE BOARD  

[8:0:66,327] The Board resolves disputes between new motor vehicle dealers and manufacturers and assists consumers in mediating  

[8:1:66,337] disputes with dealers and manufacturers.  

[8:2:66,355] 9900100 - ADMINISTRATION  

[9:0:66,373] This program provides services to support the operations of the department including executive, administrative, legal,  

[9:1:66,383] legislative, policy, and information support. Support services include accounting, budgeting, facility maintenance and  

[9:2:66,393] operations, human resources, mail operations, printing services, procurement and contracting, training, and labor relations.

[7:0:66,524] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[7:1:66,544] The Department of Motor Vehicles operates 247 facilities statewide including an estimated 1.6 million gross square feet of  

[7:2:66,554] state-owned properties and 1.2 million gross square feet of agency-leased properties. Many offices contain multiple programs,  

[7:3:66,564] which include vehicle/vessel identification and compliance, driver license and personal identification, driver safety, occupational  

[7:4:66,574] licensing and investigation. These properties support the Department's mission to serve the public by providing quality licensing  

[7:5:66,584] and motor vehicle-related services.  

[8:0:66,622] MAJOR PROJECT CHANGES  

[8:1:66,641] The Budget Act provides $88.4   million General Fund for the construction phase of office replacement projects at Delano, Santa  

[8:2:66,651] Maria, Inglewood, and Reedley; the construction phase of a reconfiguration project at Oxnard; and the performance criteria  

[8:3:66,661] phase of an on-site office replacement project at San Francisco.   Future costs to complete the San Francisco project are  

[8:4:66,671] estimated at $33.7 million.
